[01/12/24, 6:14:20â€¯PM] O2: ### **Structure of an FPGA (Field Programmable Gate Array)**

An **FPGA (Field Programmable Gate Array)** is a highly flexible, programmable semiconductor device used to implement custom digital circuits. Its structure is organized in a grid-like array of logic blocks and interconnections, allowing designers to create any digital logic design.

---

### **Key Components of FPGA Architecture**:

1. **Configurable Logic Blocks (CLBs)**:
   - The core of the FPGA.
   - Each CLB consists of:
     - **Look-Up Tables (LUTs)**: Implement combinational logic functions.
     - **Flip-Flops**: Store data for sequential logic.
     - **Multiplexers**: Route signals within the block.
   - These blocks are programmable and can implement any logic function based on the configuration.

2. **Interconnects**:
   - A network of programmable wiring connects the CLBs and I/O blocks.
   - Includes **switch matrices** to route signals between logic blocks.
   - Designers can program these interconnects to create custom pathways for signal flow.

3. **Input/Output (I/O) Blocks**:
   - Allow the FPGA to interface with external devices.
   - Programmable to handle various input and output standards (e.g., CMOS, LVTTL).
   - Located on the periphery of the FPGA.

4. **Clock Management**:
   - FPGAs include **Clock Distribution Networks** to provide synchronized clock signals to all parts of the chip.
   - Features like **Phase-Locked Loops (PLLs)** and **Clock Dividers** ensure proper timing and synchronization.

5. **Embedded Blocks**:
   - Many modern FPGAs include specialized hardware blocks like:
     - **DSP Blocks**: Perform complex arithmetic operations like multiplication.
     - **Memory Blocks (BRAM)**: Embedded RAM for storing data locally.
     - **High-Speed Transceivers**: Handle fast data communication protocols (e.g., PCIe, Ethernet).

6. **Configuration Memory**:
   - FPGAs are **programmable** because of their configuration memory, typically implemented using SRAM.
   - This memory stores the user's design and determines how CLBs, I/O blocks, and interconnects function.

---

### **Working of FPGA**:
1. **Programming**:
   - A design is created using Hardware Description Languages (HDLs) like Verilog or VHDL.
   - The design is compiled and loaded into the FPGA configuration memory.
2. **Logic Implementation**:
   - The CLBs, I/O blocks, and interconnects are configured to implement the desired circuit.
3. **Execution**:
   - Once programmed, the FPGA functions as the designed digital circuit.

---

### **Illustrative Diagram**:

Hereâ€™s a basic layout of FPGA architecture:

```
+--------------------------------------------+
|                I/O Blocks                  |
+----+---------+---------+---------+----+----+
| I/O|  CLB    |  CLB    |  CLB    |I/O |I/O |
|    |         |         |         |    |    |
+----+---------+---------+---------+----+----+
| I/O|  CLB    |  CLB    |  CLB    |I/O |I/O |
|    |         |         |         |    |    |
+----+---------+---------+---------+----+----+
|                I/O Blocks                  |
+--------------------------------------------+
```

---

### **Advantages of FPGA**:
- Highly flexible and reprogrammable.
- Parallel processing capabilities.
- Suitable for prototyping and real-time applications.

### **Applications**:
- Digital signal processing.
- Artificial intelligence and machine learning.
- Telecommunications.
- Embedded systems and hardware accelerators.

--- 

FPGAs are like blank canvases for digital logic, allowing engineers to create versatile, high-performance hardware designs tailored to specific needs.

[08/12/24, 5:53:49â€¯PM] O2: #include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

// Define the structure for a doubly linked list node
struct node {
    int data;
    struct node* next; // Pointer to the next node
    struct node* prev; // Pointer to the previous node
};

// Initialize global pointers
struct node* start = NULL;

// Function to create a doubly linked list
void Create() {
    int n, ch;
    struct node* temp;

    printf("Enter the first element: ");
    scanf("%d", &n);

    start = (struct node*)(malloc(sizeof(struct node)));
    start->data = n;
    start->next = NULL;
    start->prev = NULL;
    temp = start;

    printf("Do you want to continue? (y/n): ");
    ch = getche();

    while (ch == 'y' || ch == 'Y') {
        struct node* new1;
        printf("\nEnter the next element: ");
        scanf("%d", &n);

        new1 = (struct node*)(malloc(sizeof(struct node)));
        new1->data = n;
        new1->next = NULL;
        new1->prev = temp;

        temp->next = new1;
        temp = temp->next;

        printf("Do you want to continue? (y/n): ");
        ch = getche();
    }
}

// Function to display the doubly linked list
void Display() {
    struct node* temp;
    if (start == NULL) {
        printf("\nList not found");
    } else {
        temp = start;
        printf("\nDoubly Linked List: ");
        while (temp != NULL) {
            printf("%d\t", temp->data);
            temp = temp->next;
        }
    }
}

// Function to insert a node at the beginning
void InsertAtFirst() {
    int n;
    printf("\nEnter the element to insert at the beginning: ");
    scanf("%d", &n);

    struct node* new1 = (struct node*)(malloc(sizeof(struct node)));
    new1->data = n;
    new1->prev = NULL;
    new1->next = start;

    if (start != NULL) {
        start->prev = new1;
    }

    start = new1;
    printf("\nInserted %d at the beginning.", n);
}

// Function to insert a node at the end
void InsertAtLast() {
    int n;
    printf("\nEnter the element to insert at the end: ");
    scanf("%d", &n);

    struct node* new1 = (struct node*)(malloc(sizeof(struct node)));
    new1->data = n;
    new1->next = NULL;

    if (start == NULL) {
        new1->prev = NULL;
        start = new1;
    } else {
        struct node* temp = start;
        while (temp->next != NULL) {
            temp = temp->next;
        }
        temp->next = new1;
        new1->prev = temp;
    }

    printf("\nInserted %d at the end.", n);
}

// Function to insert a node at a specific position
void InsertAtMid() {
    int n, pos, count = 1;
    printf("\nEnter the element to insert: ");
    scanf("%d", &n);
    printf("Enter the position to insert: ");
    scanf("%d", &pos);

    if (pos == 1) {
        InsertAtFirst();
        return;
    }

    struct node* temp = start;
    struct node* new1 = (struct node*)(malloc(sizeof(struct node)));
    new1->data = n;

    while (temp != NULL && count < pos - 1) {
        temp = temp->next;
        count++;
    }

    if (temp == NULL) {
        printf("\nPosition out of range.");
        return;
    }

    new1->next = temp->next;
    new1->prev = temp;

    if (temp->next != NULL) {
        temp->next->prev = new1;
    }

    temp->next = new1;
    printf("\nInserted %d at position %d.", n, pos);
}

// Main function to test the implementation
int main() {
    int choice;

    Create();
    Display();

    while (1) {
        printf("\n\nChoose an operation:\n");
        printf("1. Insert at the beginning\n");
        printf("2. Insert at the end\n");
        printf("3. Insert in the middle\n");
        printf("4. Display list\n");
        printf("5. Exit\n");
        printf("Enter your choice: ");
        scanf("%d", &choice);

        switch (choice) {
            case 1:
                InsertAtFirst();
                break;

            case 2:
                InsertAtLast();
                break;

            case 3:
                InsertAtMid();
                break;

            case 4:
                Display();
                break;

            case 5:
                exit(0);

            default:
                printf("Invalid choice!");
        }
    }

    return 0;
}
[08/12/24, 6:40:33â€¯PM] O2: #include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

struct node {
    int data;
    struct node* next;
};

// Pointer to the first node
struct node* start = NULL;

void Create() {
    int n, ch;
    struct node *new1, *temp;

    printf("Enter the first element: ");
    scanf("%d", &n);

    // Create the first node
    start = (struct node*)malloc(sizeof(struct node));
    start->data = n;
    start->next = start;  // Point to itself to form a circle
    temp = start;

    printf("Do you want to continue? (y/n): ");
    getchar(); // To consume the newline left by scanf
    ch = getchar();  // Read the next character input

    // Loop to add more nodes
    while (ch == 'y' || ch == 'Y') {
        printf("Enter the next element: ");
        scanf("%d", &n);

        new1 = (struct node*)malloc(sizeof(struct node));
        new1->data = n;
        new1->next = start;  // Point to head to maintain circularity
        temp->next = new1;   // Update the last node's next
        temp = temp->next;   // Move temp to the new node

        printf("Do you want to continue? (y/n): ");
        getchar(); // To consume the newline left by scanf
        ch = getchar(); // Read the next character input
    }
}

void Display() {
    struct node* temp;
    
    if (start == NULL) {
        printf("List is empty.\n");
        return;
    }
    
    temp = start;
    do {
        printf("%d -> ", temp->data);
        temp = temp->next;
    } while (temp != start);
    printf("(back to start)\n");
}

int main() {
    Create();
    Display();
    return 0;
}
